<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Hunting</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Searching, pursuing, and killing wild animals</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Several terms  redirect here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hunt_(disambiguation)" title="Hunt (disambiguation)">Hunt (disambiguation)</a>, <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hunter_(disambiguation)" title="Hunter (disambiguation)">Hunter (disambiguation)</a>, <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hunters_(disambiguation)" title="Hunters (disambiguation)">Hunters (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hunting_(disambiguation)" title="Hunting (disambiguation)">Hunting (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="4800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png/220px-Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png/330px-Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png/440px-Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Childerley_driven_hunt_Finland_04.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hunter on a tree or a ground stand during a driven hunt in <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Hunting</b> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_activity" title="Human activity">human practice</a> of seeking, pursuing, capturing, or killing <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral_animal" title="Feral animal">feral animals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The most common reasons for humans to hunt are to harvest <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a> (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a>) and useful <a href="/wiki/Animal_product" title="Animal product">animal products</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fur" title="Fur">fur</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hide_(skin)" title="Hide (skin)">hide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a>/<a href="/wiki/Tusk" title="Tusk">tusks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horn_(anatomy)" title="Horn (anatomy)">horn</a>/<a href="/wiki/Antler" title="Antler">antler</a>, etc.), for <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>/<a href="/wiki/Taxidermy" title="Taxidermy">taxidermy</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">trophy hunting</a>), to remove <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">predators</a> dangerous to humans or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_animal" title="Domestic animal">domestic animals</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Wolf_hunting" title="Wolf hunting">wolf hunting</a>), to <a href="/wiki/Pest_control" title="Pest control">eliminate</a> <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuisance_animal" title="Nuisance animal">nuisance animals</a> that damage <a href="/wiki/Crop" title="Crop">crops</a>/<a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a>/<a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a> or <a href="/wiki/Zoonosis" title="Zoonosis">spread diseases</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Varmint_hunting" title="Varmint hunting">varminting</a>), for trade/tourism (see <a href="/wiki/Safari" title="Safari">safari</a>), or for <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">ecological conservation</a> against <a href="/wiki/Overpopulation" title="Overpopulation">overpopulation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a>.
</p><p>Recreationally hunted species are generally referred to as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_(food)" title="Game (food)">game</a></i>, and are usually <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>. A person participating in a hunt is a <b>hunter</b> or (less commonly)  <b>huntsman</b>; a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_area" title="Natural area">natural area</a> used for hunting is called a <a href="/wiki/Game_reserve" title="Game reserve">game reserve</a>; an experienced hunter who helps organize a hunt and/or manage the game reserve is known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamekeeper" title="Gamekeeper">gamekeeper</a>.
</p><p>Many non-human animals also hunt (see <a href="/wiki/Predation" title="Predation">predation</a>) as part of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feeding_behavior" title="Feeding behavior">feeding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parental_care" title="Parental care">parental</a> behaviors, sometimes <a href="/wiki/Surplus_killing" title="Surplus killing">in quantities exceeding immediate dietary needs</a>.  The one that does the hunting is the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">predator</a></i>, and the one being hunted is the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prey" title="Prey">prey</a></i>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bushmen_hunters_(cropped).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4698" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png/220px-Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png/330px-Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png/440px-Bushmen_hunters_%28cropped%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bushmen_hunters_(cropped).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">Bushmen</a> hunter in Botswana</div></div></div>
<p>Hunting activities by humans arose in <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> or earlier, in the order of millions of years ago.  Hunting has become deeply embedded in various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_culture" title="Human culture">human cultures</a> and was once an important part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rural" title="Rural">rural</a> economies—classified by economists as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_production_(economics)" title="Primary production (economics)">primary production</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishery" title="Fishery">fishery</a>.  Modern regulations (see <a href="/wiki/Game_law" title="Game law">game law</a>) distinguish lawful hunting activities from illegal <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a>, which involves the unauthorized and unregulated <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_animals" title="Killing of animals">killing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trapping" title="Trapping">trapping</a> or capture of animals.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG/220px-171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG/330px-171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG/440px-171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:171114-F-LS255-0011.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bowhunter" title="Bowhunter">Bowhunter</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, US</div></div></div>
<p>Apart from <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a> provision, hunting can be a means of <a href="/wiki/Population_control" title="Population control">population control</a>.  Hunting advocates state that regulated hunting can be a necessary component<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> of modern <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_management" title="Wildlife management">wildlife management</a>, for example to help maintain a healthy proportion of animal populations within an environment's ecological <a href="/wiki/Carrying_capacity" title="Carrying capacity">carrying capacity</a> when natural checks such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_predator" title="Natural predator">natural predators</a> are absent or insufficient,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> or to provide funding for <a href="/wiki/Breeding_program" title="Breeding program">breeding programs</a> and maintenance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_reserve" title="Natural reserve">natural reserves</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_area" title="Conservation area">conservation parks</a>. However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overhunting" title="Overhunting">excessive hunting</a> has also heavily contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangerment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">extirpation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> of many animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCN_Red_List_2010_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN_Red_List_2010-15">[15]</a></sup>  Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal-rights" title="Animal-rights">animal rights</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-hunting" title="Anti-hunting">anti-hunting</a> activists regard hunting as a <a href="/wiki/Cruelty_to_animals" title="Cruelty to animals">cruel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoosadism" title="Zoosadism">perverse</a> and unnecessary <a href="/wiki/Blood_sport" title="Blood sport">blood sport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-17">[17]</a></sup> Certain hunting practices, such as <a href="/wiki/Canned_hunt" title="Canned hunt">canned hunts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bidding_war" title="Bidding war">ludicrously paid</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bribery" title="Bribery">bribed</a> <a href="/wiki/Safari" title="Safari">trophy tours</a> (especially to poor countries), are considered <a href="/wiki/Fair_chase" title="Fair chase">unethical</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_exploitation" title="Economic exploitation">exploitative</a> even by some hunters.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2819" data-file-width="4799" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png/220px-Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png/330px-Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png/440px-Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Professional_stalker_standing_next_to_red_deer_stag_Ardnamurchan_Estate_Scotland_darker_01.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Professional <a href="/wiki/Deer_stalking" title="Deer stalking">deerstalker</a> standing over a downed <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red stag</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">Marine mammals</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">pinnipeds</a> are also targets of hunting, both recreationally and commercially, often with heated controversies regarding the morality, ethics and legality of such practices. The pursuit, harvesting or <a href="/wiki/Catch_and_release" title="Catch and release">catch and release</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_animal" title="Aquatic animal">aquatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cephalopod" title="Cephalopod">cephalopods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">crustaceans</a> is called <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, which however is widely accepted and not commonly categorised as a form of hunting, even though it essentially is.  It is also not considered hunting to pursue animals without intent to kill them, as in <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_photography" title="Wildlife photography">wildlife photography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatching</a>, or scientific-research activities which involve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tranquillizer_gun" title="Tranquillizer gun">tranquilizing</a> or <a href="/wiki/Electronic_tagging" title="Electronic tagging">tagging</a> of animals, although <a href="/wiki/Green_hunting" title="Green hunting">green hunting</a> is still called so.  The practices of <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_net" title="Butterfly net">netting</a> or <a href="/wiki/Insect_trap" title="Insect trap">trapping</a> <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropods</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insect_collection" title="Insect collection">trophy collection</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Foraging" title="Foraging">foraging</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">gathering</a> of <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mushroom" title="Mushroom">mushrooms</a>, are also not regarded as hunting.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg/220px-Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg/330px-Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg/440px-Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reindeer_carry_Kasper.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hunter carrying a <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a></div></div></div>
<p>Skillful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_tracking" title="Animal tracking">tracking</a> and acquisition of an elusive target has caused the word <i>hunt</i> to be used in the <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Metaphor" title="Metaphor">metaphor</a> for searching and obtaining something, as in "<a href="/wiki/Treasure_hunting" title="Treasure hunting">treasure hunting</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Discounts_and_allowances" title="Discounts and allowances">bargain</a> hunting", "<a href="/wiki/Political_campaign" title="Political campaign">hunting for votes</a>" and even "<a href="/wiki/Punishment" title="Punishment">hunting down</a>" <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The word <i>hunt</i> serves as both a <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">noun</a> ("the act of chasing game") and a <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">verb</a>. The noun has been dated to the early 12th century, from the verb <i>hunt</i>. <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> had <i>huntung</i>, <i>huntoþ</i>. The meaning of "a body of persons associated for the purpose of hunting with a pack of hounds" is first recorded in the 1570s. "The act of searching for someone or something" is from about 1600.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The verb, Old English <i>huntian</i> "to chase game" (<a href="/wiki/Transitive_verb" title="Transitive verb">transitive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intransitive_verb" title="Intransitive verb">intransitive</a>), perhaps developed from <i>hunta</i> "hunter," is related to <i>hentan</i> "to seize," from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> <i>huntojan</i> (the source also of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic</a> <i>hinþan</i> "to seize, capture," <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>hunda</i> "booty"), which is of uncertain origin. The general sense of "search diligently" (for anything) is first recorded c. 1200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Recreational hunting, also known as <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">trophy hunting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_hunting" title="Sport hunting">sport hunting</a> or "<a href="/wiki/Field_sports" title="Field sports">sporting</a>"
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_game_hunting" title="Big game hunting">Big game hunting</a>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Five_game" title="Big Five game">Big Five game</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lion_hunting" title="Lion hunting">lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elephant_hunting_in_Kenya" title="Elephant hunting in Kenya">elephant</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">buffalo</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bison_hunting" title="Bison hunting">bison</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros_poaching_in_Southern_Africa" title="Rhinoceros poaching in Southern Africa">rhinoceros</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bear_hunting" title="Bear hunting">Bear hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tiger_hunting" title="Tiger hunting">Tiger hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reindeer_hunting_in_Greenland" title="Reindeer hunting in Greenland">Caribou hunting</a></li></ul></li>
<li>Medium/small game hunting
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">Fox hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deer_hunting" title="Deer hunting">Deer hunting</a>/<a href="/wiki/Deer_stalking" title="Deer stalking">stalking</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boar_hunting" title="Boar hunting">Boar hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mink_hunting" title="Mink hunting">Mink hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coon_hunting" title="Coon hunting">Coon hunting</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fowling" title="Fowling">Fowling</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Waterfowl_hunting" title="Waterfowl hunting">Waterfowl hunting</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shorebird" title="Shorebird">Shorebird</a> hunting (<a href="/wiki/Snipe#Hunting" title="Snipe">snipe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodcock#Hunting" title="Woodcock">woodcock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curlew" title="Curlew">curlew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandpiper" title="Sandpiper">sandpiper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plover" title="Plover">plover</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Upland_hunting" title="Upland hunting">Upland hunting</a> (<a href="/wiki/Quail_hunting" title="Quail hunting">quail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pheasant_shooting" title="Pheasant shooting">pheasant</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grouse_hunting" title="Grouse hunting">grouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey_hunting" title="Turkey hunting">turkey</a>)</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pest_control" title="Pest control">Pest control</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nuisance_wildlife_management" title="Nuisance wildlife management">nuisance management</a>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">Predator</a> <a href="/wiki/Culling" title="Culling">culling</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wolf_hunting" title="Wolf hunting">Wolf hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jackal_coursing" title="Jackal coursing">Jackal coursing</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coyote#Hunting" title="Coyote">Coyote hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bobcat#Conservation" title="Bobcat">Bobcat hunting</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Varmint_hunting" title="Varmint hunting">Varmint hunting</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rabbiting" title="Rabbiting">Rabbiting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tree_squirrel#Relationship_with_humans" title="Tree squirrel">Squirrel hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rook_shooting" title="Rook shooting">Rook shooting</a></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li>Commercial hunting
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">Seal hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">Whaling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolphin_drive_hunting" title="Dolphin drive hunting">dolphin drive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dugong_hunting_in_Australia" title="Dugong hunting in Australia">dugong hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alligator_hunting" title="Alligator hunting">Alligator hunting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_meat" title="Kangaroo meat">Kangaroo hunting</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Paleolithic"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lower_to_Middle_Paleolithic">Lower to Middle Paleolithic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lower to Middle Paleolithic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hunting_hypothesis" title="Hunting hypothesis">Hunting hypothesis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Endurance_running_hypothesis" title="Endurance running hypothesis">Endurance running hypothesis</a></div>
<p>Hunting has a long history. It pre-dates the emergence of  <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" title="Anatomically modern humans">anatomically modern humans</a>) and may even predate the <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">genus</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Homo" title="Homo">Homo</a></i>.
</p><p>The oldest undisputed evidence for hunting dates to the <a href="/wiki/Early_Pleistocene" title="Early Pleistocene">Early Pleistocene</a>, consistent with the emergence and early dispersal of <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i>, about 1.7 million years ago (<a href="/wiki/Acheulean" title="Acheulean">Acheulean</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
While it is undisputed that <i>Homo erectus</i>  were hunters, the importance of this for the emergence of <i>Homo erectus</i> from its australopithecine ancestors, including the production of <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tools</a> and eventually the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_of_fire" title="Control of fire">control of fire</a>, is emphasised in the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Hunting_hypothesis" title="Hunting hypothesis">hunting hypothesis</a>" and de-emphasised in scenarios that stress omnivory and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_interaction" title="Social interaction">social interaction</a>.
</p><p>There is no direct evidence for hunting predating <i>Homo erectus</i>, in either <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_habilis" title="Homo habilis">Homo habilis</a></i> or in <i><a href="/wiki/Australopithecus" title="Australopithecus">Australopithecus</a></i>.
The early <a href="/wiki/Hominidae" title="Hominidae">hominid</a> ancestors of humans were probably <a href="/wiki/Frugivore" title="Frugivore">frugivores</a> or <a href="/wiki/Omnivore" title="Omnivore">omnivores</a>, with a partially carnivore diet from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scavenging" title="Scavenging">scavenging</a> rather than hunting.
Evidence for australopithecine meat consumption was presented in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
It has nevertheless often been assumed that at least occasional hunting behavior may have been present well before the emergence of <i>Homo</i>.
This can be argued on the basis of comparison with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">chimpanzees</a>, the closest extant relatives of humans, who also engage in hunting, indicating that the behavioral trait may have been present in the <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee%E2%80%93human_last_common_ancestor" title="Chimpanzee–human last common ancestor">Chimpanzee–human last common ancestor</a> as early as 5 million years ago. The common chimpanzee (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan_troglodytes" title="Pan troglodytes">Pan troglodytes</a></i>) regularly engages in troop predation behaviour where bands of beta males are led by an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpha_male" title="Alpha male">alpha male</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">Bonobos</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan_paniscus" title="Pan paniscus">Pan paniscus</a></i>) have also been observed to occasionally engage in group hunting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> although more rarely than <i>Pan troglodytes</i>, mainly subsisting on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frugivorous" title="Frugivorous">frugivorous</a> diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
Indirect evidence for <a href="/wiki/Oldowan" title="Oldowan">Oldowan</a> era hunting, by early <i>Homo</i> or late <i>Australopithecus</i>, has been presented in a 2009 study based on
an Oldowan site in southwestern Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Binford" title="Louis Binford">Louis Binford</a> (1986) criticised the idea that early hominids and early humans were hunters. On the basis of the analysis of the skeletal remains of the consumed animals, he concluded that hominids and early humans were mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scavengers" title="Scavengers">scavengers</a>, not hunters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
Blumenschine (1986) proposed the idea of <i>confrontational scavenging</i>, which involves challenging and scaring off other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">predators</a> <em>after</em> they have made a kill, which he suggests could have been the leading method of obtaining <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a>-rich meat by early humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Stone spearheads dated as early as 500,000 years ago were found in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Wood does not preserve well, however, and Craig Stanford, a primatologist and professor of anthropology at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>, has suggested that the discovery of spear use by chimpanzees probably means that early humans used wooden spears as well, perhaps, five million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
The earliest dated find of surviving wooden hunting <a href="/wiki/Spear" title="Spear">spears</a> dates to the very end of the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a>, just before 300,000 years ago. The <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6ningen_spears" title="Schöningen spears">Schöningen spears</a>, found in 1976 in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, are associated with <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_heidelbergensis" title="Homo heidelbergensis">Homo heidelbergensis</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hunting_hypothesis" title="Hunting hypothesis">hunting hypothesis</a> sees the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_modernity" title="Behavioral modernity">behavioral modernity</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> as directly related to hunting, including <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">mating behaviour</a>, the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a>, culture, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_religion" title="Origin of religion">religion</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythology" title="Mythology">mythology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_sacrifice" title="Animal sacrifice">animal sacrifice</a>. Sociologist <a href="/wiki/David_Nibert" title="David Nibert">David Nibert</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wittenberg_University" title="Wittenberg University">Wittenberg University</a> argues that the emergence of the organized hunting of animals undermined the communal, egalitarian nature of early human societies, with the status of women and less powerful males declining as the status of men quickly became associated with their success at hunting, which also increased human violence within these societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> However, 9000-year-old remains of a female hunter along with a toolkit of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Projectile_points" title="Projectile points">projectile points</a> and animal processing implements were discovered at the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> site of Wilamaya Patjxa, <a href="/wiki/Puno_District" title="Puno District">Puno District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Paleolithic_to_Mesolithic">Upper Paleolithic to Mesolithic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Upper Paleolithic to Mesolithic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherers" title="Hunter-gatherers">Hunter-gatherers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algerien_Desert.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1958" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Algerien_Desert.jpg/220px-Algerien_Desert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Algerien_Desert.jpg/330px-Algerien_Desert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Algerien_Desert.jpg/440px-Algerien_Desert.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algerien_Desert.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saharan_rock_art" title="Saharan rock art">Saharan rock art</a> with prehistoric archers</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="809" data-file-width="1260" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg/220px-21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg/330px-21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg/440px-21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:21_Walrus_Hunt_1999.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> hunting <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">walrus</a>, 1999</div></div></div>
<p>Evidence exists that hunting may have been one of the multiple <a href="/wiki/Environmental_factor" title="Environmental factor">environmental factors</a> leading to the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a> of <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafauna</a> and their replacement by smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbivores" title="Herbivores">herbivores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American" title="North American">North American</a> megafauna extinction was coincidental with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Younger_Dryas_impact_event" title="Younger Dryas impact event">Younger Dryas impact event</a>, possibly making hunting a less critical factor in prehistoric species loss than had been previously thought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
However, in other locations such as Australia, humans are thought to have played a very significant role in the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_megafauna" title="Australian megafauna">Australian megafauna</a> that was widespread prior to human occupation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hunting was a crucial component of hunter-gatherer societies before the <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a> of <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">dawn of agriculture</a>, beginning about 11,000 years ago in some parts of the world. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/Spear" title="Spear">spear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting_weapon" title="Hunting weapon">hunting weapons</a> developed during the Upper Paleolithic include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlatl" title="Atlatl">atlatl</a> (a spear-thrower; before 30,000 years ago) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bow_(weapon)" title="Bow (weapon)">bow</a> (18,000 years ago). By the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting_strategy" title="Hunting strategy">hunting strategies</a> had diversified with the development of these more far-reaching weapons and the <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_the_dog" title="Domestication of the dog">domestication of the dog</a> about 15,000 years ago. Evidence puts the earliest known <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">mammoth</a> hunting in Asia with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spears" title="Spears">spears</a> to approximately 16,200 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K%C3%A6rvspids,_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg/170px-K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg/255px-K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg/340px-K%C3%A6rvspids%2C_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:K%C3%A6rvspids,_Bjerlev_Hede.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sharp <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">flint</a> piece from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bjerlev_Hede&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bjerlev Hede (page does not exist)">Bjerlev Hede</a> in central Jutland. Dated around 12,500 BC and considered the oldest hunting tool from Denmark.</div></div></div>
<p>Many species of animals have been hunted throughout history. One theory is that in North America and <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">caribou and wild reindeer</a> "may well be the species of single greatest importance in the entire anthropological literature on hunting"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burch_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burch-37">[37]</a></sup> (see also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reindeer_Age" title="Reindeer Age">Reindeer Age</a>), although the varying importance of different species depended on the geographic location.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg/220px-Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg/330px-Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg/440px-Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_Figured_Olpe_depicting_the_return_of_a_hunter_and_his_dog.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient Greek <a href="/wiki/Black-figure_pottery" title="Black-figure pottery">black-figure pottery</a> depicting the return of a hunter and his dog; made in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> c. 540 BC, found in <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> hunter-gathering lifestyles remained prevalent in some parts of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, as well as all of Australia, until the European <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. They still persist in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribal_societies" title="Tribal societies">tribal societies</a>, albeit in rapid decline. Peoples that preserved Paleolithic hunting-gathering until the recent past include some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="List of indigenous peoples in Brazil">indigenous peoples of the Amazonas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ach%C3%A9" title="Aché">Aché</a>), some Central and Southern African (<a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a>), some peoples of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fayu_people" title="Fayu people">Fayu</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Mlabri_people" title="Mlabri people">Mlabri</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedda_people" title="Vedda people">Vedda people</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, and a handful of <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted peoples</a>. In Africa, one of the last remaining hunter-gatherer tribes are the <a href="/wiki/Hadza_people" title="Hadza people">Hadza</a> of Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neolithic_and_Antiquity">Neolithic and Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Neolithic and Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diana_of_Versailles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5699" data-file-width="2990" decoding="async" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Diana_of_Versailles.jpg/170px-Diana_of_Versailles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Diana_of_Versailles.jpg/255px-Diana_of_Versailles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Diana_of_Versailles.jpg/340px-Diana_of_Versailles.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diana_of_Versailles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Artemis" title="Artemis">Artemis</a> with a Hind</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> copy of an <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greek</a> sculpture, c. 325 BC, by <a href="/wiki/Leochares" title="Leochares">Leochares</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="611" data-file-width="740" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg/220px-Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg/330px-Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg/440px-Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Goguryeo_tomb_mural.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of a <a href="/wiki/Goguryeo_tombs" title="Goguryeo tombs">Goguryeo tomb mural</a> of hunting, middle of the first millennium</div></div></div>
<p>Even as <a href="/wiki/Domestication#Animals" title="Domestication">animal domestication</a> became relatively widespread and after the development of agriculture, hunting was usually a significant contributor to the human food supply.
The supplementary meat and materials from hunting included <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a> for implements, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinew" title="Sinew">sinew</a> for <a href="/wiki/Rope" title="Rope">cordage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fur" title="Fur">fur</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feathers" title="Feathers">feathers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rawhide_(textile)" title="Rawhide (textile)">rawhide</a> and leather used in clothing.
</p><p>Hunting is still vital in marginal climates, especially those unsuited for <a href="/wiki/Pastoral" title="Pastoral">pastoral</a> uses or agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> trap and hunt animals for clothing and use the skins of <a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">sea mammals</a> to make <a href="/wiki/Kayak" title="Kayak">kayaks</a>, clothing, and footwear.
</p><p>On ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliefs" title="Reliefs">reliefs</a>, especially from <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, kings are often depicted as hunters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_game_hunting" title="Big game hunting">big game</a> such as lions and are often portrayed hunting from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_chariot" title="War chariot">war chariot</a>. The cultural and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological" title="Psychological">psychological</a> importance of hunting in ancient societies is represented by deities such as <a href="/wiki/Horned_God" title="Horned God">the horned god</a> <a href="/wiki/Cernunnos" title="Cernunnos">Cernunnos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lunar_deity" title="Lunar deity">lunar goddesses</a> of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>, the Greek <a href="/wiki/Artemis" title="Artemis">Artemis</a> or Roman <a href="/wiki/Diana_(mythology)" title="Diana (mythology)">Diana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">Taboos</a> are often related to hunting, and mythological association of prey species with a <a href="/wiki/Divinity" title="Divinity">divinity</a> could be reflected in hunting restrictions such as a <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">reserve</a> surrounding a temple. <a href="/wiki/Euripides" title="Euripides">Euripides</a>' tale of Artemis and <a href="/wiki/Actaeon" title="Actaeon">Actaeon</a>, for example, may be seen as a caution against disrespect of prey or impudent boasting.
</p><p>With the domestication of the dog, <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey">birds of prey</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ferret" title="Ferret">ferret</a>, various forms of animal-aided hunting developed, including <a href="/wiki/Medieval_hunting" title="Medieval hunting">venery</a> (<a href="/wiki/Scent_hound" title="Scent hound">scent hound</a> hunting, such as <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a>), <a href="/wiki/Coursing" title="Coursing">coursing</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sight_hound" title="Sight hound">sight hound</a> hunting), <a href="/wiki/Falconry" title="Falconry">falconry</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferreting" title="Ferreting">ferreting</a>. While these are all associated with <a href="/wiki/Medieval_hunting" title="Medieval hunting">medieval hunting</a>, over time, various <a href="/wiki/Dog_breed" title="Dog breed">dog breeds</a> were selected for very precise tasks during the hunt, reflected in such names as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pointing_breed" title="Pointing breed">pointer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Setter" title="Setter">setter</a>.
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lion_hunting" title="Lion hunting">Lion hunting</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pastoral_and_agricultural_societies">Pastoral and agricultural societies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pastoral and agricultural societies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1465" data-file-width="1435" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png/220px-Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png/330px-Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png/440px-Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nobleman_in_Hunting_Costume_preceded_by_his_Servant_trying_to_find_the_Scent_of_a_Stag.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobleman" title="Nobleman">Nobleman</a> in hunting costume with his servant following the scent of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stag" title="Stag">stag</a>, 14th century</div></div></div>
<p>Even as agriculture and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a> became more prevalent, hunting often remained as a part of human culture where the environment and social conditions allowed. Hunter-gatherer societies persisted, even when increasingly confined to marginal areas. And within agricultural systems, hunting served to kill animals that prey upon <a href="/wiki/List_of_domesticated_animals" title="List of domesticated animals">domestic and wild animals</a> or to attempt to <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">extirpate</a> animals seen by humans as competition for resources such as water or forage.
</p><p>When hunting moved from a subsistence activity to a selective one, two trends emerged:
</p>
<ol><li>the development of the role of the specialist hunter, with special training and equipment</li>
<li>the option of hunting as a "sport" for members of an upper social class</li></ol>
<p>The meaning of the word <i>game</i> in <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a> evolved to include an animal which is hunted. As the domestication of animals for meat grew, subsistence hunting remained among the lowest classes; however, the stylised pursuit of game in European societies became a luxury. Dangerous hunting, such as for lions or <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boars</a>, often done on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horseback" title="Horseback">horseback</a> or from a <a href="/wiki/Chariot" title="Chariot">chariot</a>, had a function similar to <a href="/wiki/Tournament_(medieval)" title="Tournament (medieval)">tournaments</a> and manly sports. Hunting ranked as an honourable, somewhat competitive pastime to help the <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a> practice skills of war in times of peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>In most parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">medieval</a> Europe, the upper class obtained the sole rights to hunt in certain areas of a feudal territory. Game in these areas was used as a source of food and furs, often provided via professional huntsmen, but it was also expected to provide a form of recreation for the aristocracy. The importance of this proprietary view of game can be seen in the <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a> legends, in which one of the primary charges against the outlaws is that they "hunt the King's deer". In contrast, settlers in Anglophone colonies gloried democratically in hunting for all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>In medieval Europe, hunting was considered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johannes_Scotus_Eriugena" title="Johannes Scotus Eriugena">Johannes Scotus Eriugena</a> to be part of the set of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanic_arts" title="Mechanic arts">seven mechanical arts</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_dog">Use of dog</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Use of dog">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3974" data-file-width="5406" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg/220px-%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg/330px-%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg/440px-%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27Jachtgezellen%27_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1023.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Hunting Companions</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> 19th-century painting featuring two dogs, a <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotgun</a> and a game bag</div></div></div>
<p>Although various other animals have been used to aid the hunter, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferrets" title="Ferrets">ferrets</a>, the dog has assumed many very important uses to the hunter.
The domestication of the dog has led to a <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiotic relationship</a> in which the dog's independence from humans is deferred. Though dogs can survive independently of humans, and in many cases do ferrally, when raised or adopted by humans the species tends to defer to its control in exchange for habitation, food and support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>Dogs today are used to find, chase, retrieve, and sometimes kill game. Dogs allow humans to pursue and kill prey that would otherwise be very difficult or dangerous to hunt. Different breeds of specifically bred <a href="/wiki/Hunting_dog" title="Hunting dog">hunting dog</a> are used for different types of hunting. Waterfowl are commonly hunted using retrieving dogs such as the <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Retriever" title="Labrador Retriever">Labrador Retriever</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Retriever" title="Golden Retriever">Golden Retriever</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Retriever" title="Chesapeake Bay Retriever">Chesapeake Bay Retriever</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brittany_Spaniel" title="Brittany Spaniel">Brittany Spaniel</a>, and other similar breeds. <a href="/wiki/Upland_game_bird" title="Upland game bird">Game birds</a> are flushed out using flushing <a href="/wiki/Spaniel" title="Spaniel">spaniels</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/English_Springer_Spaniel" title="English Springer Spaniel">English Springer Spaniel</a>, the various <a href="/wiki/Cocker_Spaniel" title="Cocker Spaniel">Cocker Spaniels</a> and similar breeds.
</p><p>The hunting of wild mammals in England and Wales with dogs was banned under the <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act 2004</a>. The wild mammals include fox, hare, deer and mink.  There are, however, exceptions in the Act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Homo_Necans" title="Homo Necans">Homo Necans</a></div>
<p>Many prehistoric deities are depicted as predators or prey of humans, often in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoomorphic" title="Zoomorphic">zoomorphic</a> form, perhaps alluding to the importance of hunting for most Palaeolithic cultures.
</p><p>In many pagan religions, specific rituals are conducted before or after a hunt; the rituals done may vary according to the species hunted or the season the hunt is taking place.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Often a hunting ground, or the hunt for one or more species, was reserved or prohibited in the context of a temple cult.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In Roman religion, <a href="/wiki/Diana_(mythology)" title="Diana (mythology)">Diana</a> is the goddess of the hunt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CheetahHunt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="988" data-file-width="1419" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CheetahHunt.jpg/220px-CheetahHunt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CheetahHunt.jpg/330px-CheetahHunt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/CheetahHunt.jpg/440px-CheetahHunt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CheetahHunt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aristocrat" title="Aristocrat">aristocrats</a> hunting a <a href="/wiki/Blackbuck" title="Blackbuck">blackbuck</a> alongside an <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah" title="Asiatic cheetah">Asiatic cheetah</a>, 1812</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_and_Eastern_religions">Indian and Eastern religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Indian and Eastern religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output
