<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sikh_Hunting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sikh_Hunting.jpg/220px-Sikh_Hunting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sikh_Hunting.jpg/330px-Sikh_Hunting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sikh_Hunting.jpg/440px-Sikh_Hunting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sikh_Hunting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a> hunting (Unknown <a href="/wiki/Pahari_painting" title="Pahari painting">Pahari artist</a>, 18th century)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar,_Rohtak_District,_Panjab.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1958" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg/220px-A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg/330px-A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg/440px-A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar%2C_Rohtak_District%2C_Panjab.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_tiger_hunt_at_Jhajjar,_Rohtak_District,_Panjab.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tiger hunt at Jhajjar, Rohtak District, Punjab, c. 1820</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu_scripture" title="Hindu scripture">Hindu scriptures</a> describe hunting as an occupation, as well as a sport of the kingly. Even figures considered divine are described to have engaged in hunting. One of the names of the god <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a> is Mrigavyadha, which translates as "the deer hunter" (<i>mriga</i> means deer; <i>vyadha</i> means hunter). The word <i>Mriga</i>, in many Indian languages including Malayalam, not only stands for deer, but for all animals and animal instincts (Mriga Thrishna). Shiva, as Mrigavyadha, is the one who destroys the animal instincts in human beings. In the epic <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dasharatha" title="Dasharatha">Dasharatha</a>, the father of <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Rama</a>, is said to have the ability to hunt in the dark. During one of his hunting expeditions, he accidentally killed <a href="/wiki/Shravana" title="Shravana">Shravana</a>, mistaking him for game. During Rama's exile in the forest, <a href="/wiki/Ravana" title="Ravana">Ravana</a> kidnapped his wife, <a href="/wiki/Sita" title="Sita">Sita</a>, from their hut, while Rama was asked by Sita to capture a golden deer, and his brother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakshman" title="Lakshman">Lakshman</a> went after him. According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahabharat" title="Mahabharat">Mahabharat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandu" title="Pandu">Pandu</a>, the father of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pandavas" title="Pandavas">Pandavas</a>, accidentally killed the sage Kindama and his wife with an arrow, mistaking them for a deer. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> teaches followers to have tremendous respect for all of life. Prohibitions for hunting and meat eating are the fundamental conditions for being a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jain" title="Jain">Jain</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>'s first <a href="/wiki/Precept" title="Precept">precept</a> is the respect for all sentient life. The general approach by all Buddhists is to avoid killing any living animals. <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Buddha</a> explained the issue by saying "all fear death; comparing others with oneself, one should neither kill nor cause to kill."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Inline_citation#When_you_must_use_inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Inline citation"><span title="The text near this tag needs a citation. (August 2022)">quote citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, only meat obtained from hunting, or slaughtered with the <a href="/wiki/Jhatka" title="Jhatka">Jhatka</a> is permitted. The <a href="/wiki/Sikh_gurus" title="Sikh gurus">Sikh gurus</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Guru_Hargobind" title="Guru Hargobind">Guru Hargobind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guru_Gobind_Singh" title="Guru Gobind Singh">Guru Gobind Singh</a> were ardent hunters. Many old Sikh <a href="/wiki/Sikh_Rehat_Maryada" title="Sikh Rehat Maryada">Rehatnamas</a> like <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prem_Sumarag&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prem Sumarag (page does not exist)">Prem Sumarag</a>, recommend hunting <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>. However, among modern Sikhs, the practise of hunting has died down; some even saying that all meat is forbidden.
</p>
<h3><span id="Christianity.2C_Judaism.2C_and_Islam"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity,_Judaism,_and_Islam">Christianity, Judaism, and Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Christianity, Judaism, and Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ladies_Hunting.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1663" data-file-width="2303" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ladies_Hunting.png/220px-Ladies_Hunting.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ladies_Hunting.png/330px-Ladies_Hunting.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ladies_Hunting.png/440px-Ladies_Hunting.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ladies_Hunting.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ladies hunting in the 15th century</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="692" data-file-width="781" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg/220px-Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg/330px-Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg/440px-Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flanders_Tapestry_with_the_hunting_scene.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tapestry" title="Tapestry">Tapestry</a> with a hunting scene, late 16th century</div></div></div>
<p>From <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Christian" title="Early Christian">early Christian</a> times, hunting has been forbidden to Roman Catholic Church <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleric" title="Cleric">clerics</a>. Thus the <i><a href="/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Canonici" title="Corpus Juris Canonici">Corpus Juris Canonici</a></i> (C. ii, X, De cleric. venat.) says, "We forbid to all servants of God hunting and expeditions through the woods with hounds; and we also forbid them to keep hawks or falcons." The <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Council_of_the_Lateran" title="Fourth Council of the Lateran">Fourth Council of the Lateran</a>, held under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Innocent_III" title="Pope Innocent III">Pope Innocent III</a>, decreed (canon xv): "We interdict hunting or hawking to all clerics." The decree of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> is worded more mildly: "Let clerics abstain from illicit hunting and hawking" (Sess. XXIV, De reform., c. xii), which seems to imply that not all hunting is illicit, and canonists generally make a distinction declaring noisy (<i>clamorosa</i>) hunting unlawful, but not quiet (<i>quieta</i>) hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ferraris gives it as the general sense of canonists that hunting is allowed to clerics if it be indulged in rarely and for sufficient cause, as necessity, utility or "honest" recreation, and with that moderation which is becoming to the ecclesiastical state. Ziegler, however, thinks that the interpretation of the canonists is not in accordance with the letter or spirit of the laws of the church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nevertheless, although a distinction between lawful and unlawful hunting<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> is undoubtedly permissible, it is certain that a bishop can absolutely prohibit all hunting to the clerics of his diocese, as was done by <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">synods</a> at <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, and elsewhere. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedict_XIV" title="Benedict XIV">Benedict XIV</a> declared that such synodal decrees are not too severe, as an absolute prohibition of hunting is more conformable to the <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">ecclesiastical law</a>. In practice, therefore, the synodal statutes of various localities must be consulted to discover whether they allow quiet hunting or prohibit it altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-:3-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Jewish law hunting is not forbidden although there is an aversion to it. The great 18th-century authority <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rabbi_Yechezkel_Landau" title="Rabbi Yechezkel Landau">Rabbi Yechezkel Landau</a> after a study concluded although "hunting would not be considered cruelty to animals insofar as the animal is generally killed quickly and not tortured... There is an unseemly element in it, namely cruelty." The other issue is that hunting can be dangerous and Judaism places an extreme emphasis on the value of human life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>Islamic <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia Law</a> permits hunting of lawful animals and birds if they cannot be easily caught and slaughtered. However, this is only for the purpose of food and not for trophy hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_traditions">National traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: National traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ST-bakerelephant.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" data-file-width="660" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ST-bakerelephant.jpg/220px-ST-bakerelephant.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ST-bakerelephant.jpg/330px-ST-bakerelephant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ST-bakerelephant.jpg/440px-ST-bakerelephant.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ST-bakerelephant.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Explorer and big game hunter <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Baker" title="Samuel Baker">Samuel Baker</a> chased by an elephant, illustration from 1890</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Safari" title="Safari">Safari</a></div>
<p>A safari, from a <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> word meaning "a long journey", especially in Africa, is defined as an overland journey. Safari as a distinctive way of hunting was popularized by the US author <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a> and President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> A safari may consist of a several-days—or even weeks-long journey, with <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_bush" title="The bush">the bush</a> or <a href="/wiki/Jungle" title="Jungle">jungle</a>, while pursuing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_(food)" title="Game (food)">big game</a>. Nowadays, it is often used to describe tours through African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_African_national_parks" title="List of African national parks">national parks</a> to watch or hunt wildlife.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Hunters are usually tourists, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Hunting_license" title="Hunting license">licensed</a> and highly <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">regulated</a> professional hunters, local guides, <a href="/wiki/Skinner_(profession)" title="Skinner (profession)">skinners</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Porter_(carrier)" title="Porter (carrier)">porters</a> in more difficult terrains. A special safari type is the solo-safari, where all the license acquiring, stalking, preparation, and outfitting is done by the hunter himself.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Indian subcontinent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="712" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg/220px-Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg/330px-Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg/440px-Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Weeks_Edwin_Departure_For_The_Hunt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Edwin_Lord_Weeks" title="Edwin Lord Weeks">Weeks Edwin's</a> painting <i>Departure for the Hunt</i>, c. 1885</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="648" data-file-width="976" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg/220px-Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg/330px-Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg/440px-Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hunting_party_mandalay1885.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i>Shikar</i> party in <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>, soon after the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Burmese_War" title="Third Anglo-Burmese War">Third Anglo-Burmese War</a> in 1886, when Burma was annexed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Indian_feudalism" title="Indian feudalism">feudal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_India" title="Colonial India">colonial</a> times in <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>, hunting or <i>shikar</i> was regarded as a regal sport in the numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princely_states" title="Princely states">princely states</a>, as many <a href="/wiki/Maharaja" title="Maharaja">maharajas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nawab" title="Nawab">nawabs</a>, as well as British officers, maintained a whole corps of <i>shikari</i>s (<a href="/wiki/Big-game_hunting" title="Big-game hunting">big-game hunters</a>), who were native professional hunters. They would be headed by a master of the hunt, who might be styled <i>mir-shikar</i>. Often, they recruited the normally low-ranking local tribes because of their <a href="/wiki/Traditional_knowledge" title="Traditional knowledge">traditional knowledge</a> of the environment and hunting techniques. Big game, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengal_tigers" title="Bengal tigers">Bengal tigers</a>, might be hunted from the back of an <a href="/wiki/Indian_elephant" title="Indian elephant">Indian elephant</a>.
</p><p>Regional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norm_(sociology)" title="Norm (sociology)">social norms</a> are generally antagonistic to hunting, while a few <a href="/wiki/Sect" title="Sect">sects</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bishnoi" title="Bishnoi">Bishnoi</a>, lay special emphasis on the conservation of particular species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelope</a>. India's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildlife_Protection_Act_of_1972" title="Wildlife Protection Act of 1972">Wildlife Protection Act of 1972</a> bans the killing of all wild animals. However, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Forest_Service" title="Indian Forest Service">Chief Wildlife Warden</a> may, if satisfied that any wild animal from a specified list has become dangerous to human life, or is so disabled or diseased as to be beyond recovery, permit any person to hunt such an animal. In this case, the body of any wild animal killed or wounded becomes government property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>The practice among the soldiers in British India during the 1770s of going out to hunt <a href="/wiki/Snipe" title="Snipe">snipes</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shorebird" title="Shorebird">shorebird</a> considered extremely challenging for hunters due to its alertness, camouflaging color and erratic flight behavior, is believed to be the origin of the modern word for <a href="/wiki/Sniper" title="Sniper">sniper</a>, as snipe-hunters needed to be stealthy in addition to having <a href="/wiki/Tracking_(hunting)" title="Tracking (hunting)">tracking</a> skills and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marksmanship" title="Marksmanship">marksmanship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-:10-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etymology_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-etymology-54">[54]</a></sup> The term was used in the nineteenth century, and had become common usage by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Snowden_Slights,_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1754" data-file-width="1404" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg/220px-Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg/330px-Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg/440px-Snowden_Slights%2C_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Snowden_Slights,_front_view_YORYM-S13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Snowden Slights with <a href="/wiki/Retriever" title="Retriever">retriever</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotgun</a> around 1910, 'the last of Yorkshire's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildfowler" title="Wildfowler">Wildfowlers</a>'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blast_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blast-55">[55]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hunting_and_shooting_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Hunting and shooting in the United Kingdom">Hunting and shooting in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Deer_stalking" title="Deer stalking">Deer stalking</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_hunting_legislation" title="Fox hunting legislation">Fox hunting legislation</a></div><p>
Unarmed <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a> on horseback with hounds is the type of hunting most closely associated with the United Kingdom; in fact, "hunting" without qualification implies fox hunting. What in other countries is called "hunting" is called "shooting" (birds) or "stalking" (deer) in Britain. Originally a form of <a href="/wiki/Vermin" title="Vermin">vermin</a> control to protect livestock, fox hunting became a popular social activity for newly wealthy upper classes in <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian times</a> and a traditional rural activity for riders and foot followers alike. Similar to fox hunting in many ways is the chasing of hares with <a href="/wiki/Hound" title="Hound">hounds</a>. Pairs of <a href="/wiki/Sighthound" title="Sighthound">sighthounds</a> (or long-dogs), such as <a href="/wiki/Greyhound" title="Greyhound">greyhounds</a>, may be used to pursue a hare in coursing, where the greyhounds are marked as to their skill in coursing the hare (but are not intended to actually catch it), or the hare may be pursued with <a href="/wiki/Scent_hound" title="Scent hound">scent hounds</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Beagle" title="Beagle">beagles</a> or harriers. Other sorts of <a href="/wiki/Foxhound" title="Foxhound">foxhounds</a> may also be used for hunting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stag" title="Stag">stags (deer)</a> or <a href="/wiki/American_mink" title="American mink">mink</a>. <a href="/wiki/Deer_stalking" title="Deer stalking">Deer stalking</a> with rifles is carried out on foot without hounds, using stealth.</p><div style="clear:left;"></div>
<p>These forms of hunting have been controversial in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Animal_welfare" title="Animal welfare">Animal welfare</a> supporters believe that hunting causes unnecessary suffering to foxes, horses, and hounds. Proponents argue that it is culturally and perhaps economically important. Using dogs to chase wild mammals was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_hunting_legislation" title="Fox hunting legislation">made illegal</a> in February 2005 by the <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act 2004</a>; there were a number of exemptions (under which the activity may not be illegal) in the act for hunting with hounds, but no exemptions at all for hare-coursing.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_traditions">Shooting traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Shooting traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Game birds, especially <a href="/wiki/Pheasant" title="Pheasant">pheasants</a>, are shot with shotguns for sport in the UK; the <a href="/wiki/British_Association_for_Shooting_and_Conservation" title="British Association for Shooting and Conservation">British Association for Shooting and Conservation</a> says that over a million people per year participate in shooting, including game shooting, <a href="/wiki/Clay_pigeon_shooting" title="Clay pigeon shooting">clay pigeon shooting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shooting_sports" title="Shooting sports">target shooting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
Shooting as practised in Britain, as opposed to traditional hunting, requires little questing for game—around thirty-five million birds are released onto shooting estates every year, some having been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Factory_farming" title="Factory farming">factory farmed</a>. Shoots can be elaborate affairs with guns placed in assigned positions and assistants to help load shotguns. When in position, "beaters" move through the areas of cover, swinging sticks or flags to drive the game out. Such events are often called "drives". The open season for <a href="/wiki/Grouse" title="Grouse">grouse</a> in the UK begins on 12 August, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Twelfth" title="Glorious Twelfth">Glorious Twelfth</a>. The definition of game in the United Kingdom is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Game_Act_1831" title="Game Act 1831">Game Act 1831</a>.
</p><p>A similar tradition, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ojeo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ojeo (page does not exist)">ojeo</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/ojeo" title="es:ojeo">es</a>]</sup></i>, exists in Spain.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake,_ME.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="651" data-file-width="885" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg/220px-Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg/330px-Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg/440px-Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake%2C_ME.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Camp_on_Schoodic_Lake,_ME.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hunting camp with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_dressing_deer" title="Field dressing deer">dressed deer</a> at Schoodic Lake, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, in 1905</div></div></div>

style="width:174px;max-width:174px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image"
