the <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Archipelago" title="Kodiak Archipelago">Kodiak Archipelago</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>North American hunting pre-dates the United States by thousands of years and was an important part of many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">pre-Columbian</a> Native American cultures. Native Americans retain some hunting rights and are exempt from some laws as part of Indian treaties and otherwise under <a href="/wiki/Federal_law" title="Federal law">federal law</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>—examples include <a href="/wiki/Eagle_feather_law" title="Eagle feather law">eagle feather laws</a> and exemptions in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_Mammal_Protection_Act_of_1972" title="Marine Mammal Protection Act of 1972">Marine Mammal Protection Act</a>. This is considered particularly important in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" title="Alaska Native">Alaskan native</a> communities.
</p><p>Hunting is primarily regulated by <a href="/wiki/State_law_(United_States)" title="State law (United States)">state law</a>; additional regulations are imposed through <a href="/wiki/United_States_environmental_law" title="United States environmental law">United States environmental law</a> in the case of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Migratory_birds" title="Migratory birds">migratory birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a>. Regulations vary widely from state to state and govern the areas, time periods, techniques and methods by which specific game animals may be hunted. Some states make a distinction between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protected_species" title="Protected species">protected species</a> and unprotected species (often <a href="/wiki/Vermin" title="Vermin">vermin</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varmint" title="Varmint">varmints</a> for which there are no hunting regulations). Hunters of protected species require a <a href="/wiki/Hunting_license" title="Hunting license">hunting license</a> in all states, for which completion of a hunting safety course is sometimes a prerequisite.
</p><p>Typically, game animals are divided into several categories for regulatory purposes. Typical categories, along with example species, are as follows:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Big game</i>: <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">white-tailed deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mule_deer" title="Mule deer">mule deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elk" title="Elk">elk</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribou" title="Caribou">caribou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bear" title="Bear">bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bighorn_sheep" title="Bighorn sheep">bighorn sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pronghorn" title="Pronghorn">pronghorn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boar" title="Boar">boar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Javelina" title="Javelina">javelina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bison" title="Bison">bison</a></li>
<li><i>Small game</i>: <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a>, hare, <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">raccoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porcupine" title="Porcupine">porcupine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skunk" title="Skunk">skunk</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ring-tailed_cat" title="Ring-tailed cat">ring-tailed cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">armadillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruffed_grouse" title="Ruffed grouse">ruffed grouse</a></li>
<li><i>Furbearers</i>: <a href="/wiki/Beaver" title="Beaver">beaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">mink</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pine_marten" title="Pine marten">pine marten</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musk_rat" title="Musk rat">musk rat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otter" title="Otter">otter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a></li>
<li><i>Predators</i>: <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">cougar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" title="Gray wolf">wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Upland_game_bird" title="Upland game bird">Upland game bird</a></i>: <a href="/wiki/Grouse" title="Grouse">grouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodcock" title="Woodcock">woodcock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chukar_partridge" title="Chukar partridge">chukar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pheasant" title="Pheasant">pheasant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quail" title="Quail">quail</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dove" title="Dove">dove</a></li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterfowl" title="Waterfowl">Waterfowl</a></i>: <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">duck</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_teal" title="Common teal">teal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merganser" title="Merganser">merganser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">geese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swan" title="Swan">swan</a></li></ul>
<p>Hunting big game typically requires a "tag" for each animal harvested. Tags must be purchased in addition to the hunting license, and the number of tags issued to an individual is typically limited. In cases where there are more prospective hunters than the quota for that species, tags are usually assigned by lottery. Tags may be further restricted to a specific area, or wildlife management unit. <a href="/wiki/Waterfowl_hunting" title="Waterfowl hunting">Hunting migratory waterfowl</a> requires a duck stamp from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">Fish and Wildlife Service</a> in addition to the appropriate state hunting license.
</p><p>Harvest of animals other than big game is typically restricted by a bag limit and a possession limit. A bag limit is the maximum number of a specific animal species that an individual can harvest in a single day. A possession limit is the maximum number of a specific animal species that can be in an individual's possession at any time.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting">Shooting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shooting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hectors_photos_109.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Hectors_photos_109.JPG/220px-Hectors_photos_109.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Hectors_photos_109.JPG/330px-Hectors_photos_109.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Hectors_photos_109.JPG/440px-Hectors_photos_109.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hectors_photos_109.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A man target practicing for the hunting seasons</div></div></div>
<p>Gun usage in hunting is typically regulated by game category, area within the state, and time period. Regulations for <a href="/wiki/Big-game_hunting" title="Big-game hunting">big-game hunting</a> often specify a minimum <a href="/wiki/Caliber" title="Caliber">caliber</a> or <a href="/wiki/Muzzle_energy" title="Muzzle energy">muzzle energy</a> for <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a>. The use of <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> is often banned for safety reasons in areas with high <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population densities</a> or limited <a href="/wiki/Terrain" title="Terrain">topographic relief</a>. Regulations may also limit or ban the use of <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> because of environmental concerns. Specific seasons for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bow_(weapon)" title="Bow (weapon)">bow</a> hunting or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muzzle-loader" title="Muzzle-loader">muzzle-loading</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_powder" title="Black powder">black-powder</a> guns are often established to limit competition with hunters using more effective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons" title="Weapons">weapons</a>.
</p><p>Hunting in the United States is not associated with any particular class or culture; a 2006 poll showed seventy-eight percent of Americans supported legal hunting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> although relatively few Americans actually hunt. At the beginning of the 21st century, just six percent of Americans hunted. <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southerners</a> in states along the eastern seaboard hunted at a rate of five percent, slightly below the national average, and while hunting was more common in other parts of the South at nine percent, these rates did not surpass those of the Plains states, where twelve percent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midwesterners" title="Midwesterners">Midwesterners</a> hunted. Hunting in other areas of the country fell below the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Overall, in the 1996–2006 period, the number of hunters over the age of sixteen declined by ten percent, a drop attributable to a number of factors including <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat loss</a> and changes in recreation habits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation">Regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Regulation of hunting within the United States dates from the 19th century. Some modern hunters see themselves as <a href="/wiki/Conservation_movement" title="Conservation movement">conservationists</a> and sportsmen in the mode of <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boone_and_Crockett_Club" title="Boone and Crockett Club">Boone and Crockett Club</a>. Local hunting clubs and national organizations provide hunter education and help protect the future of the sport by buying land for future hunting use. Some groups represent a specific hunting interest, such as <a href="/wiki/Ducks_Unlimited" title="Ducks Unlimited">Ducks Unlimited</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pheasants_Forever" title="Pheasants Forever">Pheasants Forever</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Waterfowl_Foundation" title="Delta Waterfowl Foundation">Delta Waterfowl Foundation</a>. Many hunting groups also participate in lobbying the federal government and state government.
</p><p>Each year, nearly $200 million in hunters' federal excise taxes are distributed to state agencies to support wildlife management programs, the purchase of lands open to hunters, and hunter education and safety classes. Since 1934, the sale of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Duck_Stamp" title="Federal Duck Stamp">Federal Duck Stamps</a>, a required purchase for migratory <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterfowl" title="Waterfowl">waterfowl</a> hunters over sixteen years old, has raised over $700 million to help purchase more than 5,200,000 acres (8,100 sq mi; 21,000 km<sup>2</sup>) of habitat for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Wildlife_Refuge_System" title="National Wildlife Refuge System">National Wildlife Refuge System</a> lands that support waterfowl and many other wildlife species and are often open to hunting. States also collect money from hunting licenses to assist with management of game animals, as designated by law. A key task of federal and state <a href="/wiki/Park_ranger" title="Park ranger">park rangers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_warden" title="Game warden">game wardens</a> is to enforce laws and regulations related to hunting, including species protection, <a href="/wiki/Hunting_season" title="Hunting season">hunting seasons</a>, and hunting bans.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Varmint_hunting">Varmint hunting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Varmint hunting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Varmint_hunting" title="Varmint hunting">Varmint hunting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1560" data-file-width="2035" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg/180px-Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg/270px-Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg/360px-Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myocastor_coypus_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coypu" title="Coypu">coypu</a> is hunted as a pest in Louisiana.</div></div></div>
<p>Varmint hunting is an American phrase for the selective killing of non-game animals seen as pests. While not always an efficient form of <a href="/wiki/Pest_control" title="Pest control">pest control</a>, varmint hunting achieves selective control of pests while providing recreation and is much less regulated. Varmint species are often responsible for detrimental effects on crops, livestock, <a href="/wiki/Landscaping" title="Landscaping">landscaping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, and pets. Some animals, such as wild rabbits or squirrels, may be utilised for fur or meat, but often no use is made of the carcass. Which species are varmints depends on the circumstance and area. Common varmints may include various <a href="/wiki/Rodent" title="Rodent">rodents</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coyotes" title="Coyotes">coyotes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corvus_(genus)" title="Corvus (genus)">crows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral_cats" title="Feral cats">feral cats</a>, and feral <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">hogs</a>. Some animals once considered varmints are now protected, such as wolves. In the US state of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">non-native</a> rodent, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coypu" title="Coypu">coypu</a>, has become so destructive to the local ecosystem that the state has initiated a <a href="/wiki/Bounty_(reward)" title="Bounty (reward)">bounty</a> program to help control the population. <a href="/wiki/Beaver_eradication_in_Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Beaver eradication in Tierra del Fuego">Beavers from North America constitute an invasive species</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>, where eradication attempts are ongoing.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fair_chase">Fair chase</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Fair chase">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fair_chase" title="Fair chase">Fair chase</a></div>
<p>The principles of the <a href="/wiki/Fair_chase" title="Fair chase">fair chase</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> have been a part of the American hunting tradition for over one hundred years. The role of the hunter-conservationist, popularised by Theodore Roosevelt, and perpetuated by Roosevelt's formation of the <a href="/wiki/Boone_and_Crockett_Club" title="Boone and Crockett Club">Boone and Crockett Club</a>, has been central to the development of the modern fair chase tradition. <i>Beyond Fair Chase: The Ethic and Tradition of Hunting</i>, a book by Jim Posewitz, describes fair chase:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Fundamental to ethical hunting is the idea of fair chase. This concept addresses the balance between the hunter and the hunted. It is a balance that allows hunters to occasionally succeed while animals generally avoid being taken."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Internet_hunting" title="Internet hunting">Internet hunting</a> was introduced in 2005, allowing people to hunt over the Internet using remotely controlled guns, the practice was widely criticised by hunters as violating the principles of fair chase. As a representative of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Rifle_Association_of_America" title="National Rifle Association of America">National Rifle Association of America</a> (NRA) explained, "The NRA has always maintained that fair chase, being in the field with your firearm or bow, is an important element of hunting tradition. Sitting at your desk in front of your computer, clicking at a mouse, has nothing to do with hunting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HSUS-FactSheet_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-HSUS-FactSheet-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="615" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg/260px-Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg/390px-Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg/520px-Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bear-hunters-kephart-nc1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hunters with an <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">American black bear</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains" title="Great Smoky Mountains">Great Smoky Mountains</a></div></div></div>
<p>One hunting club declares that a fair chase shall not involve the taking of animals under the following conditions:
</p>
<ul><li>Helpless in a trap, deep snow or water, or on ice.</li>
<li>From any power vehicle or power boat.</li>
<li>By "<a href="/wiki/Spotlighting" title="Spotlighting">jacklighting</a>" or shining at night.</li>
<li>By the use of any tranquilizers or poisons.</li>
<li>While inside escape-proof fenced enclosures.</li>
<li>By the use of any power vehicle or power boat for herding or driving animals, including use of aircraft to land alongside or to communicate with or direct a hunter on the ground.</li>
<li>By the use of electronic devices for attracting, locating or pursuing game or guiding the hunter to such game, or by the use of a bow or arrow to which any electronic device is attached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranches">Ranches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ranches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Animals such as <a href="/wiki/Blackbuck" title="Blackbuck">blackbuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nilgai" title="Nilgai">nilgai</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_deer" title="Axis deer">axis deer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">fallow deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zebra" title="Zebra">zebras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barasingha" title="Barasingha">barasingha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelle</a> and many other exotic game species can now be found on <a href="/wiki/Game_farm" title="Game farm">game farm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ranch" title="Ranch">ranches</a> in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, where they were introduced for sport hunting. These hunters can be found paying in excess of $10,000 dollars to take trophy animals on these controlled ranches.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hunting_in_Russia" title="Hunting in Russia">Hunting in Russia</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> imperial hunts evolved from hunting traditions of early Russian rulers—<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Prince" title="Grand Prince">Grand Princes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Czar" title="Russian Czar">Tsars</a>—under the influence of hunting customs of European royal courts. The imperial hunts were organised mainly in <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">Peterhof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsarskoye_Selo" title="Tsarskoye Selo">Tsarskoye Selo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gatchina" title="Gatchina">Gatchina</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven,_ca._1936.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="694" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg/220px-StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg/330px-StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg/440px-StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven%2C_ca._1936.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StateLibQld_1_140043_Riders_gather_for_a_dingo_drive_at_Durella_Station_in_Morven,_ca._1936.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Riders gather for a <a href="/wiki/Dingo" title="Dingo">dingo</a> drive in <a href="/wiki/Morven,_Queensland" title="Morven, Queensland">Morven, Queensland</a>, 1936</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hunting_in_Australia" title="Hunting in Australia">Hunting in Australia</a></div>
<p>Hunting in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> has evolved around the hunting and eradication of various animals considered to be pests or <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a> .  All native animals are protected by law, and certain species such as <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">kangaroos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">ducks</a> can be hunted by <a href="/wiki/Hunting_license" title="Hunting license">licensed</a> shooters but only under a special permit on <a href="/wiki/Public_land" title="Public land">public lands</a> during <a href="/wiki/Hunting_season" title="Hunting season">open seasons</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced species</a> that are targeted include <a href="/wiki/European_rabbit" title="European rabbit">European rabbits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red foxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sambar_deer" title="Sambar deer">sambar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hog_deer" title="Hog deer">hog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">fallow</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chital_deer" title="Chital deer">chital</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rusa_deer" title="Rusa deer">rusa</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feral_cats_in_Australia" title="Feral cats in Australia">feral cats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feral_pig#Australia" title="Feral pig">pigs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feral_goats_in_Australia" title="Feral goats in Australia">goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brumby" title="Brumby">brumbies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feral_donkeys_in_Australia" title="Feral donkeys in Australia">donkeys</a> and occasionally <a href="/wiki/Australian_feral_camel" title="Australian feral camel">camels</a>, as well as introduced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upland_bird" title="Upland bird">upland birds</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Quail" title="Quail">quails</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pheasant" title="Pheasant">pheasants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partridge" title="Partridge">partridges</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hunting_in_New_Zealand" title="Hunting in New Zealand">Hunting in New Zealand</a></div>
<p>New Zealand has a strong hunting culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> When humans arrived, the only mammals present on the islands making up New Zealand were bats, although seals and other marine mammals were present along the coasts. However, when humans arrived they brought other species with them. Polynesian voyagers introduced kuri (dogs), kiore (Polynesian rats), as well as a range of plant species.  European explorers further added to New Zealand's biota, particularly pigs which were introduced by either Captain Cook or the French explorer De Surville in the 1700s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> During the nineteenth century, as European colonisation took place, <a href="/wiki/Acclimatisation_society" title="Acclimatisation society">acclimatisation societies</a> were established.  The societies introduced a large number of species with no use other than as prey for hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Species that adapted well to the New Zealand terrain include <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pigs" title="Pigs">pigs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goats" title="Goats">goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hare" title="Hare">hare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahr" title="Tahr">tahr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chamois" title="Chamois">chamois</a>. With wilderness areas, suitable forage, and no natural predators, their populations exploded. Government agencies view the animals as pests due to their effects on the <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">natural environment</a> and on agricultural production, but hunters view them as a resource.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Iranian tradition regarded hunting as an essential part of a prince's education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and hunting was well recorded for the education of the upper-class youths during <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran#Classical_antiquity" title="History of Iran">pre-Islamic Persia</a>. As of October 2020, a hunting licence costs $20,000. The Department of Environment although do not report the number of permits issued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The numbers of licensed hunters in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, including those using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snare_trap" title="Snare trap">snares</a> and guns, is generally decreasing, while their average age is increasing. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were approximately 190,000 registered hunters, approximately 65% of whom were sixty years old or older.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a very active tradition of hunting small to medium-sized wild game in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. Hunting is carried out with firearms, slingshots and cage traps, and sometimes aided by the use of hounds. The illegal use of trap guns and snare nets also occurs. With approximately 12,000 to 13,000 hunters applying for and being granted hunting permits in recent years, there is some concern that the practice might not be sustainable. In addition there are at present no bag limits and the open season is comparatively very long (5 months – October to February inclusive). As such hunting pressure from legal hunters is very high. Added to that, there is a thriving and very lucrative black market for poached wild game (sold and enthusiastically purchased as expensive luxury delicacies) and the numbers of commercial poachers in operation is unknown but presumed to be fairly high. As a result, the populations of the five major mammalian game species (<a href="/wiki/Red-rumped_agouti" title="Red-rumped agouti">red-rumped agouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowland_paca" title="Lowland paca">lowland paca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nine-banded_armadillo" title="Nine-banded armadillo">nine-banded armadillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collared_peccary" title="Collared peccary">collared peccary</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_brocket_deer" title="Red brocket deer">red brocket deer</a>) are thought to be relatively low when compared to less-hunted regions in nearby mainland <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> (although scientifically conducted population studies are only just recently being conducted as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>). It appears that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_brocket_deer" title="Red brocket deer">red brocket deer</a> population has been extirpated in <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> as a result of over-hunting. By some time in the mid 20th century another extirpation due to over-hunting occurred in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> with its population of <a href="/wiki/Horned_screamer" title="Horned screamer">horned screamer</a> (a large game bird). Various herons, ducks, doves, the <a href="/wiki/Green_iguana" title="Green iguana">green iguana</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryptic_golden_tegu" title="Cryptic golden tegu">cryptic golden tegu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_caiman" title="Spectacled caiman">spectacled caiman</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Common_opossum" title="Common opossum">common opossum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Capybara" title="Capybara">capybara</a> are also commonly hunted and poached. There is also some poaching of 'fully protected species', including <a href="/wiki/Guyanan_red_howler" title="Guyanan red howler">red howler</a> monkey and <a href="/wiki/Capuchin_monkey" title="Capuchin monkey">capuchin monkeys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_tamandua" title="Southern tamandua">southern tamandua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_porcupine" title="Brazilian porcupine">Brazilian porcupine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow-footed_tortoise" title="Yellow-footed tortoise">yellow-footed tortoise</a>, the critically endangered island endemic <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_piping_guan" title="Trinidad piping guan">Trinidad piping guan</a> and even one of the national birds, the <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_ibis" title="Scarlet ibis">scarlet ibis</a>. Legal hunters pay relatively small fees to obtain hunting licences and undergo no official basic <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation biology</a> or hunting-ethics/<a href="/wiki/Fair_chase" title="Fair chase">fair chase</a> training, and are not assessed regarding their knowledge and comprehension of the local wildlife conservation laws. There is presumed to be relatively little subsistence hunting in the country (with most hunting for either sport or commercial profit). The local wildlife management authorities are under-staffed and under-funded, and as such little in the way of enforcement is done to uphold existing wildlife management laws, with hunting/poaching occurring both in and out of season and even in wildlife sanctuaries. There is some indication that the government is beginning to take the issue of wildlife management more seriously, with well drafted legislation being brought before Parliament in 2015. It remains to be seen if the drafted legislation will be fully adopted and financially supported by the current and future governments, and if the general populace will move towards a greater awareness of the importance of wildlife conservation and change the culture of wanton consumption to one of sustainable management.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_management">Wildlife management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Wildlife management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Weisergatter.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="866" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Weisergatter.png/220px-Weisergatter.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Weisergatter.png/330px-Weisergatter.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Weisergatter.png/440px-Weisergatter.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Weisergatter.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Control fence to assess the impact of <a href="/wiki/Browsing_(herbivory)" title="Browsing (herbivory)">browsing</a> by <a href="/wiki/Ungulate" title="Ungulate">ungulates</a>. Note the lack of natural forest regeneration outside the fencing.</div></div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_management" title="Wildlife management">Wildlife management</a></div>
<p>Hunting is claimed to give <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_management" title="Wildlife management">resource managers</a> an important tool<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> in managing populations that might exceed the <a href="/wiki/Carrying_capacity" title="Carrying capacity">carrying capacity</a> of their <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a> and threaten the well-being of other species, or, in some instances, damage human health or safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>In some cases, hunting actually can increase the population of predators such as coyotes by removing territorial bounds that would otherwise be established, resulting in excess neighbouring migrations into an area, thus artificially increasing the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Hunting advocates<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2012)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> assert that hunting reduces <a href="/wiki/Intraspecific_competition" title="Intraspecific competition">intraspecific competition</a> for food and shelter, reducing mortality among the remaining animals. Some <a href="/wiki/Environmentalist" title="Environmentalist">environmentalists</a> assert<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2009)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> that (re)introducing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Predator" title="Predator">predators</a> would achieve the same end with greater efficiency and less negative effect, such as introducing significant amounts of free <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a> into the environment and <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">food chain</a>.
</p><p>In the United States, wildlife managers are frequently part of hunting regulatory and licensing bodies, where they help to set rules on the number, manner and conditions in which game may be hunted.
</p><p>Management agencies sometimes rely on hunting to control specific animal populations, as has been the case with deer in North America. These hunts may sometimes be carried out by professional shooters, although others may include amateur hunters. Many US city and local governments hire professional and amateur hunters each year to reduce populations of animals such as deer that are becoming hazardous in a restricted area, such as neighbourhood parks and <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan</a> open spaces.
</p><p>A large part of managing populations involves managing the number and, sometimes, the size or age of animals harvested so as to ensure the sustainability of the population. Tools that are frequently used to control harvest are bag limits and season closures, although gear restrictions such as archery-only seasons are becoming increasingly popular in an effort to reduce hunter success rates in countries that rely on bag limits per hunter instead of per area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws">Laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunting_legislation" title="Hunting legislation">Hunting legislation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">Poaching</a></div>
<p>Illegal hunting and harvesting of wild species contrary to local and international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_(ethic)" title="Conservation (ethic)">conservation</a> and wildlife management laws is called poaching. <a href="/wiki/Game_preservation" title="Game preservation">Game preservation</a> is one of the tactics used to prevent poaching. Violations of hunting laws and regulations involving poaching are normally punishable by law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Punishment can include <a href="/wiki/Confiscation" title="Confiscation">confiscation of equipment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fine_(penalty)" title="Fine (penalty)">fines</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prison</a> sentence.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Right_to_hunt"><span class="anchor" id="right_to_hunt"></span>Right to hunt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Right to hunt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The right to hunt—sometimes in combination with the right to fish—is protected implicitly, as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Property_rights_(economics)" title="Property rights (economics)">right of ownership</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> or explicitly, as a <a href="/wiki/Rights" title="Rights">right</a> on its own,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-81">[81]</a></sup> in a number of jurisdictions. For instance, as of 2019, a total of 22 U.S. states explicitly recognize a subjective right to hunt in their constitutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bag_limits">Bag limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Bag limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bag_limits" title="Bag limits">Bag limits</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg/220px-Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg/330px-Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg/440px-Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bird_shooting_game_rack.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Red-legged_partridge" title="Red-legged partridge">Red-legged partridges</a> on a game rack</div></div></div>
<p>Bag limits are provisions under the law that control how many animals of a given species or group of species can be killed, although there are often species for which bag limits do not apply. There are also <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">jurisdictions</a> where bag limits are not applied at all or are not applied under certain circumstances. The phrase <i>bag limits</i> comes from the custom among hunters of small game to carry successful kills in a small basket, similar to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fishing_creel" title="Fishing creel">fishing creel</a>.
</p><p>Where bag limits are used, there can be daily or seasonal bag limits; for example, ducks can often be harvested at a rate of six per hunter per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Big game, like <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, most often have a seasonal bag limit of one animal per hunter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Bag limits may also regulate the size, sex, or age of animal that a hunter can kill. In many cases, bag limits are designed to allocate harvest among the hunting population more equitably rather than to protect animal populations, as protecting the population would necessitate regional density-dependent maximum bags.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closed_and_open_season">Closed and open season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Closed and open season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closed_season" title="Closed season">closed season</a> is a time during which hunting an animal of a given species is contrary to law. Typically, closed seasons are designed to protect a species when they are most vulnerable or to protect them during their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breeding_season" title="Breeding season">breeding season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> By extension, the period that is not the closed season is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_season_(hunting)" title="Open season (hunting)">open season</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">Methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg/220px-Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg/330px-Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg/440px-Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bechuana_hunting_the_lion-1841.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tswana hunting the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, 1841</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1005" data-file-width="1799" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg/220px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg/330px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg/440px-Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Jacob_Miller_-_Hunting_Buffalo_-_Walters_371940190.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American <a href="/wiki/Bison" title="Bison">bison</a> being chased off a cliff as seen and painted by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Jacob_Miller" title="Alfred Jacob Miller">Alfred Jacob Miller</a>, c. 1860</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BedaleHunt2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="875" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BedaleHunt2005.jpg/220px-BedaleHunt2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BedaleHunt2005.jpg/330px-BedaleHunt2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BedaleHunt2005.jpg/440px-BedaleHunt2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BedaleHunt2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Master or whipper-in and fox hounds drawing a wood. Hunting in Yorkshire, northern England, in 2005, on the last day of fully legal, proper, fox hunting.</div></div></div>
<p>Historical, subsistence, and sport hunting techniques can differ radically, with modern hunting regulations often addressing issues of where, when, and how hunts are conducted. Techniques may vary depending on government regulations, a hunter's personal ethics, local custom, hunting equipment, and the animal being hunted. Often a hunter will use a combination of more than one technique. Laws may forbid sport hunters from using some methods used primarily in poaching and wildlife management.
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Bait_(luring_substance)" title="Bait (luring substance)">Baiting</a></i> is the use of <a href="/wiki/Decoy" title="Decoy">decoys</a>, lures, scent, or food.</li>
<li><i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/battue" title="wikt:battue">Battue</a></i> involves scaring animals (by beating sticks) into a killing zone or ambush.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Beagling" title="Beagling">Beagling</a></i> is the use of <a href="/wiki/Beagle" title="Beagle">beagles</a> in hunting <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbits</a>, and sometimes in hunting <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">foxes</a>.</li>
<li><i>Beating</i> uses human beaters to flush out game from an area or drive it into position.</li>
<li><i>Stand hunting</i> or <i>blind hunting</i> is waiting for animals from a concealed or elevated position, for example from <a href="/wiki/Tree_stand" title="Tree stand">tree stands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting_blind" title="Hunting blind">hunting blinds</a> or other types of shooting stands.</li>
<li><i>Calling</i> is the use of animal noises to attract or drive animals.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Camouflage" title="Camouflage">Camouflage</a></i> is the use of visual or odour concealment to blend with the environment.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hunting_dog" title="Hunting dog">Dogs</a></i> may be used to <a href="/wiki/Coursing" title="Coursing">course</a> or to help flush, herd, drive, track, point at, pursue, or retrieve prey.</li>
<li><i>Driving</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Herding" title="Herding">herding</a> of animals in a particular direction, usually toward another hunter in the group.</li>
<li><i>Flushing</i> is the practice of scaring animals from concealed areas.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ghillie_suit" title="Ghillie suit">Ghillie suit</a></i> is a type of gear a person can wear to blend with environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Glassing</i> is the use of optics, such as binoculars, to locate animals more easily.</li>
<li><i>Glue</i> is an indiscriminate passive form to kill birds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Internet_hunting" title="Internet hunting">Internet hunting</a></i> is a method of hunting over the Internet using <a href="/wiki/Webcam" title="Webcam">webcams</a> and remotely controlled guns.</li>
<li><i><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1023754711">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="Netting"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Netting</span></span></i> involves using <a href="/wiki/Net_(device)" title="Net (device)">nets</a>, including active netting with the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannon_netting" title="Cannon netting">cannon nets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocket_net" title="Rocket net">rocket nets</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Persistence_hunting" title="Persistence hunting">Persistence hunting</a></i> is the use of running and tracking to pursue the prey to exhaustion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Posting</i> is done by sitting or standing in a particular place with the intentions of intercepting your game of choice along their travel corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Scouting</i> for game is typically done prior to a hunt and will ensure the desired species are in a chosen area.  Looking for animal sign such as tracks, scat, etc.... and utilizing "trail cameras" are commonly used tactics while scouting.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Shooting" title="Shooting">Shooting</a></i> is the use of a ranged weapon such as a gun, bow, crossbow, or slingshot.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Solunar_theory" title="Solunar theory">Solunar theory</a></i> says that animals move according to the location of the moon in comparison to their bodies and is said to have been used long before this by hunters to know the best times to hunt their desired game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Spotlighting" title="Spotlighting">Spotlighting</a></i> or <i>shining</i> is the use of artificial light to find or blind animals before killing.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Game_stalker" title="Game stalker">Stalking</a></i> or <i>still hunting</i> is the practice of walking quietly in search of animals or in pursuit of an individual animal.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Tracking_(hunting)" title="Tracking (hunting)">Tracking</a></i> is the practice of reading physical evidence in pursuing animals.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_trapping" title="Animal trapping">Trapping</a></i> is the use of devices such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snare_trap" title="Snare trap">snares</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trapping_pit" title="Trapping pit">pits</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deadfall_trap" title="Deadfall trap">deadfalls</a> to capture or kill an animal.</li></ul>
