<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graph">Graph</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Graph">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg"><img alt="Bar graph - Number of hunters in various countries.svg" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1761" decoding="async" height="698" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg/1200px-Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg/1800px-Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg/2400px-Bar_graph_-_Number_of_hunters_in_various_countries.svg.png 2x" width="1200"/></a>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy_hunting">Trophy hunting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Trophy hunting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">Trophy hunting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usov.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Usov.jpg/170px-Usov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Usov.jpg/255px-Usov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Usov.jpg/340px-Usov.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Usov.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trophy collection of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princely_Family_of_Liechtenstein" title="Princely Family of Liechtenstein">Princely Family of Liechtenstein</a> at <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Asov" title="Úsov">Úsov</a> Château, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_(3).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2965" data-file-width="4567" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg/220px-Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg/330px-Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg/440px-Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zdravko_Pe%C4%8Dar_During_an_Elephant_Hunt_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hunter and local guides with an <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephant</a> they shot, 1970</div></div></div>
<p>Trophy hunting is the selective seeking and killing of wild game animals to take <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trophies" title="Trophies">trophies</a> for <a href="/wiki/Private_collection" title="Private collection">personal collection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boasting" title="Boasting">bragging rights</a> or as a <a href="/wiki/Status_symbol" title="Status symbol">status symbol</a>.  It may also include the controversial hunting of captive or semi-captive animals expressly bred and raised under controlled or semi-controlled conditions so as to attain trophy characteristics; this is sometimes known as <a href="/wiki/Canned_hunt" title="Canned hunt">canned hunts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 19th century, southern and central European sport hunters often pursued game only for a <a href="/wiki/Trophy" title="Trophy">trophy</a>, usually the head or <a href="/wiki/Fur" title="Fur">pelt</a> of an animal, which was then displayed as a sign of prowess. The rest of the animal was typically discarded. Some cultures, however, disapprove of such waste. In <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, hunting for trophies was—and still is—frowned upon. Hunting in North America in the 19th century was done primarily as a way to supplement food supplies, although it is now undertaken mainly for sport.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hunting#Africa" title="Hunting">safari</a> method of hunting was a development of sport hunting that saw elaborate travel in Africa, India and other places in pursuit of trophies. In modern times, <a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">trophy hunting</a> persists and is a significant industry in some areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_tool">Conservation tool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Conservation tool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service">U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service</a>, hunting "provides an economic incentive" for ranchers to continue to breed those species, and that hunting "reduces the threat of the species' extinction."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>A scientific study in the journal, <i>Biological Conservation</i>, states that trophy hunting is of "major importance to conservation in Africa by creating economic incentives for conservation over vast areas, including areas which may be unsuitable for alternative wildlife-based land uses such as photographic ecotourism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africanwildlifeconservationfund.org_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-africanwildlifeconservationfund.org-98">[98]</a></sup> However, another study states that less than 3% of a trophy hunters' expenditures reach the local level, meaning that the economic incentive and benefit is "minimal, particularly when we consider the vast areas of land that hunting concessions occupy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economistsatlarge_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-economistsatlarge-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>Financial incentives from trophy hunting effectively more than double the land area that is used for wildlife conservation, relative to what would be conserved relying on national parks alone according to <i>Biological Conservation</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africanwildlifeconservationfund.org_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-africanwildlifeconservationfund.org-98">[98]</a></sup> although local communities usually derive no more than 18 cents per hectare from trophy hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economistsatlarge_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-economistsatlarge-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trophy_hunting" title="Trophy hunting">Trophy hunting</a> has been considered essential for providing economic incentives to conserve large carnivores according to research studies in <i>Conservation Biology</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs.umn.edu_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbs.umn.edu-100">[100]</a></sup> <i>Journal of Sustainable Tourism</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> <i>Wildlife Conservation by Sustainable Use</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and <i>Animal Conservation</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs.umn.edu_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbs.umn.edu-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Studies by the Centre for Responsible Tourism<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> and the IUCN state that ecotourism, which includes more than hunting, is a superior economic incentive, generating twice the revenue per acre and 39 times more permanent employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> At the crosssection of trophy hunting, ecotourism and conservation is <a href="/wiki/Green_hunting" title="Green hunting">green hunting</a>, a trophy hunting alternative where hunters pay to dart animals that need to be tranquilized for conservation projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_Committee_on_Natural_Resources" title="U.S. House Committee on Natural Resources">U.S. House Committee on Natural Resources</a> in 2016 concluded that trophy hunting may be contributing to the extinction of certain animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Animal welfare organizations, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFAW" title="IFAW">International Fund for Animal Welfare</a>, claim that trophy hunting is a key factor in the "silent extinction" of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giraffes" title="Giraffes">giraffes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a national survey that the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service conducts every five years, fewer people are hunting, even as population rises. National Public Radio reported, a graph shows 2016 statistics, that only about 5 percent of Americans, 16 years old and older, actually hunt, which is half of what it was 50 years ago. The decline in popularity of hunting is expected to accelerate over the next decade, which threatens how US will pay for conservation.
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_Cecil_the_lion" title="Killing of Cecil the lion">Killing of Cecil the lion</a></div>
<p>Trophy hunting is most often criticised when it involves rare or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endangered" title="Endangered">endangered</a> animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Opponents may also see trophy hunting as an issue of <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">morality</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Cruelty_to_animals" title="Cruelty to animals">animal cruelty</a>, criticising the killing of living creatures for <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>. <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> dramatist <a href="/wiki/W._S._Gilbert" title="W. S. Gilbert">W. S. Gilbert</a> remarked, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deer-stalking" title="Deer-stalking">Deer-stalking</a> would be a very fine sport if only the deer had guns."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is also debate about the extent to which trophy hunting benefits the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_economy" title="Local economy">local economy</a>. Hunters pay substantial fees to the game outfitters and hunting guides which contributes to the local economy and provides value to animals that would otherwise be seen as competition for grazing, livestock, and crops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> However, the argument is disputed by animal welfare organizations and other opponents of trophy hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> It is argued that the animals are worth more to the community for <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> than hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg/220px-AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg/330px-AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg/440px-AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AM_Hunting_Lodge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chatelherault_Country_Park" title="Chatelherault Country Park">Chatelherault</a>, built by <a href="/wiki/William_Adam_(architect)" title="William Adam (architect)">William Adam</a> in 1743 as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Douglas-Hamilton,_5th_Duke_of_Hamilton" title="James Douglas-Hamilton, 5th Duke of Hamilton">Duke of Hamilton's</a> hunting lodge</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1098" data-file-width="1459" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG/220px-Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG/330px-Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG/440px-Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mannerheim_hunting_house.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marshal%27s_Cabin" title="Marshal's Cabin">Marshal's Cabin</a>, a former hunting lodge in <a href="/wiki/Loppi" title="Loppi">Loppi</a>, Finland</div></div></div>
<p>A variety of industries benefit from hunting and support hunting on economic grounds. In <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, it is estimated that a safari hunter spends fifty to one hundred times that of the average <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecotourist" title="Ecotourist">ecotourist</a>. While the average photo tourist may seek luxury accommodation, the average safari hunter generally stays in tented camps. Safari hunters are also more likely to use remote areas, uninviting to the typical ecotourist. Advocates argue that these hunters allow for anti-poaching activities and revenue for local communities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In the United Kingdom, the game hunting of birds as an industry is said to be extremely important to the rural economy. The Cobham Report of 1997 suggested it to be worth around £700 million, and hunting and shooting lobby groups claimed it to be worth over a billion pounds less than ten years later.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Hunting also has a significant financial impact in the United States, with many companies specialising in hunting <a href="/wiki/Sports_equipment" title="Sports equipment">equipment</a> or speciality tourism. Many different technologies have been created to assist hunters. Today's hunters come from a broad range of economic, social, and cultural backgrounds. In 2001, over thirteen million hunters averaged eighteen days hunting, and spent over $20.5 billion on their sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In the US, proceeds from hunting licences contribute to state game management programs, including preservation of wildlife habitat.
</p><p>Hunting contributes to a portion of caloric intake of people and may have positive impacts on greenhouse gas emissions by avoidance of utilization of meat raised under industrial methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:40SW.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/40SW.jpg/220px-40SW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/40SW.jpg/330px-40SW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/40SW.jpg/440px-40SW.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:40SW.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Right: <a href="/wiki/.40_S%26W" title=".40 S&amp;W">.40 S&amp;W</a> round with <a href="/wiki/Hollow-point_bullet" title="Hollow-point bullet">hollow-point bullet</a>, Left: expanded bullet of the same calibre with exposed lead core</div></div></div>
<p>Lead bullets that miss their target or remain in an unretrieved carcass could become a <a href="/wiki/Toxicant" title="Toxicant">toxicant</a> in the environment but lead in ammunition because of its metallic form has a lower solubility and higher resistance to corrosion than other forms of lead making it hardly available to biological systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Waterfowl or other birds may ingest the lead and poison themselves with the neurotoxicant, but studies have demonstrated that effects of lead in ammunition are negligible on animal population size and growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Since 1991, US federal law forbids lead shot in waterfowl hunts, and 30 states have some type of restriction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ps1013_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-ps1013-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, a federal appeals court denied a lawsuit by environmental groups that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EPA" title="EPA">EPA</a> must use the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toxic_Substances_Control_Act" title="Toxic Substances Control Act">Toxic Substances Control Act</a> to regulate lead in shells and cartridges. The groups sought EPA to regulate "spent lead", yet the court found EPA could not regulate spent lead without also regulating cartridges and shells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-we1214_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-we1214-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_(ethic)" title="Conservation (ethic)">Conservation (ethic)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservation_movement" title="Conservation movement">Conservation movement</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2012</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unbalanced plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-unbalanced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">unbalanced</a> towards certain viewpoints</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit">improve the article</a> by adding information on neglected viewpoints, or discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hunting" title="Talk:Hunting">talk page</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2012</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1363" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg/220px-Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg/330px-Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg/440px-Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paulus_Potter_-_Punishment_of_a_Hunter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Punishment of a Hunter</i> (c. 1647) by <a href="/wiki/Paulus_Potter" title="Paulus Potter">Paulus Potter</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hunters have been driving forces throughout history in the movement to ensure the preservation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" title="Habitat (ecology)">wildlife habitats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> for further hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> However, excessive hunting and poachers have also contributed heavily to the endangerment, extirpation and extinction of many animals, such as the <a href="/wiki/Quagga" title="Quagga">quagga</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_auk" title="Great auk">great auk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_cow" title="Steller's sea cow">Steller's sea cow</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thylacine" title="Thylacine">thylacine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bluebuck" title="Bluebuck">bluebuck</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tiger" title="Caspian tiger">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javan_tiger" title="Javan tiger">Javan tigers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Markhor" title="Markhor">markhor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_rhinoceros" title="Sumatran rhinoceros">Sumatran rhinoceros</a>, the bison, the <a href="/wiki/North_American_cougar" title="North American cougar">North American cougar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Altai_argali" title="Altai argali">Altai argali</a> sheep, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a> and many more, primarily for commercial sale or sport. All these animals have been hunted to <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangerment</a> or extinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Poaching currently threatens bird and mammalian populations around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The 2019 <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Assessment_Report_on_Biodiversity_and_Ecosystem_Services" title="Global Assessment Report on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services">Global Assessment Report on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services</a></i> lists the direct exploitation of organisms, including hunting, as the second leading cause of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a>, after land use for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2022, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPBES" title="IPBES">IPBES</a> released another report which stated that unsustainable hunting, along with unsustainable logging and fishing, are primary drivers of the global extinction crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Pittman.E2.80.93Robertson_Wildlife_Restoration_Act_of_1937"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pittman–Robertson_Wildlife_Restoration_Act_of_1937">Pittman–Robertson Wildlife Restoration Act of 1937</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Pittman–Robertson Wildlife Restoration Act of 1937">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1937, American hunters successfully lobbied the US Congress to pass the <a href="/wiki/Pittman%E2%80%93Robertson_Federal_Aid_in_Wildlife_Restoration_Act" title="Pittman–Robertson Federal Aid in Wildlife Restoration Act">Pittman-Robertson Wildlife Restoration Act</a>, which placed an eleven percent tax on all hunting equipment. This self-imposed tax now generates over $700 million each year and is used exclusively to establish, restore and protect wildlife habitats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The act is named for Nevada Senator <a href="/wiki/Key_Pittman" title="Key Pittman">Key Pittman</a> and Virginia Congressman <a href="/wiki/Absalom_Willis_Robertson" title="Absalom Willis Robertson">Absalom Willis Robertson</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_Duck_Stamp_program">Federal Duck Stamp program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Federal Duck Stamp program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 16 March 1934, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">President Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> signed the Migratory Bird Hunting Stamp Act, which requires an annual stamp purchase by all hunters over the age of sixteen. The stamps are created on behalf of the program by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Postal_Service" title="US Postal Service">US Postal Service</a> and depict wildlife artwork chosen through an annual contest. They play an important role in <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">habitat conservation</a> because ninety-eight percent of all funds generated by their sale go directly toward the purchase or lease of <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetland</a> habitat for protection in the <a href="/wiki/National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="National Wildlife Refuge">National Wildlife Refuge System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In addition to waterfowl, it is estimated that one third of the nation's endangered species seek food and shelter in areas protected using Duck Stamp funds.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Since 1934, the sale of Federal Duck Stamps has generated $670 million, and helped to purchase or lease 5,200,000 acres (8,100 sq mi; 21,000 km<sup>2</sup>) of habitat. The stamps serve as a license to hunt migratory birds, an entrance pass for all National Wildlife Refuge areas, and are also considered collectors items often purchased for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aesthetic" title="Aesthetic">aesthetic</a> reasons outside of the hunting and birding communities. Although non-hunters buy a significant number of Duck Stamps, eighty-seven percent of their sales are contributed by hunters. Distribution of funds is managed by the Migratory Bird Conservation Commission (MBCC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Species">Species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arabian_oryx">Arabian oryx</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Arabian oryx">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a>, a species of large <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelope</a>, once inhabited much of the desert areas of the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talbot,_Lee_Merriam_1960_pp._84_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Talbot,_Lee_Merriam_1960_pp._84-131">[131]</a></sup> However, the species' striking appearance made it (along with the closely related scimitar-horned oryx and addax) a popular quarry for sport hunters, especially foreign executives of oil companies working in the region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The use of automobiles and high-powered rifles destroyed their only advantage: speed, and they became extinct in the wild exclusively due to sport hunting in 1972. The scimitar-horned oryx followed suit, while the addax became critically endangered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> However, the Arabian oryx has now made a comeback and been upgraded from "extinct in the wild" to "vulnerable" due to conservation efforts like captive breeding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Markhor">Markhor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Markhor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Markhor" title="Markhor">markhor</a> is an endangered species of wild goat which inhabits the mountains of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a> of these regions by <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> gave British sport hunters access to the species, and they were hunted heavily, almost to the point of extinction. Only their willingness to breed in captivity and the inhospitability of their mountainous habitat prevented this. Despite these factors, the markhor is still endangered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_bison">American bison</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: American bison">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_bison" title="American bison">American bison</a> is a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovid" title="Bovid">bovid</a> which inhabited much of western North America prior to the 1800s, living on the prairies in large herds. However, the vast herds of bison attracted market hunters, who killed dozens of bison for their hides only, leaving the rest to rot. Thousands of these hunters quickly eliminated the bison herds, bringing the population from several million in the early 1800s to a few hundred by the 1880s. Conservation efforts have allowed the population to increase, but the bison remains near-threatened due to lack of habitat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="White_rhino">White rhino</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: White rhino">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Journal of International Wildlife Law and Policy</i> cites that the legalization of white rhinoceros hunting in South Africa motivated private landowners to reintroduce the species onto their lands. As a result, the country saw an increase in white rhinos from fewer than one hundred individuals to more than 11,000, even while a limited number were killed as trophies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the illegal hunting of rhinoceros for their horns is highly damaging to the population and is currently growing globally,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> with 1004 being killed in South Africa alone according to the most recent estimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The White Rhino (along with the other 4 rhino species) are poached due to beliefs that the Rhinos horns can be used to cure Cancer, Arthritis and other diseases and illnesses, even though they are scientifically proven wrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_species">Other species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Other species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Richard_Conniff" title="Richard Conniff">Richard Conniff</a>, Namibia is home to 1,750 of the roughly 5,000 black rhinos surviving in the wild because it allows trophy hunting of various species. Namibia's mountain zebra population has increased to 27,000 from 1,000 in 1982. Elephants, which "are gunned down elsewhere for their ivory", have gone to 20,000 from 15,000 in 1995. Lions, which were on the brink of extinction "from Senegal to Kenya", are increasing in Namibia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>In contrast, Botswana in 2012 banned trophy hunting following a precipitous wildlife decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> The numbers of antelope plummeted across Botswana, with a resultant decline in predator numbers, while elephant numbers remained stable and hippopotamus numbers rose. According to the government of Botswana, trophy hunting is at least partly to blame for this, but many other factors, such as poaching, drought and habitat loss are also to blame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Uganda recently did the same, arguing that "the share of benefits of sport hunting were lopsided and unlikely to deter poaching or improve [Uganda's] capacity to manage the wildlife reserves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In 2020, Botswana reopened trophy hunting on public lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Studies">Studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cage_trap_on_a_farm,_Namibia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2819" data-file-width="4415" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg/220px-Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg/330px-Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg/440px-Cage_trap_on_a_farm%2C_Namibia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cage_trap_on_a_farm,_Namibia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cage <a href="/wiki/Trapping#Trap_types" title="Trapping">trap</a> (<a href="/wiki/Trapping#Cage_traps_(live_traps)" title="Trapping">live trap</a>) for <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">cheetahs</a> on a farm in <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a></div></div></div>
<p>A study published by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildlife_Society" title="Wildlife Society">Wildlife Society</a> concluded that hunting and trapping are cost effective tools that reduce wildlife damage by reducing a population below the capacity of the environment to carry it and changing the behaviors of animals to stop them from causing damage. The study furthermore states that the cessation of hunting could cause wildlife to be severely harmed, rural property values to fall, and the incentive of landowners to maintain natural habitats to diminish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although deforestation and forest degradation have long been considered the most significant threats to tropical biodiversity, across Southeast Asia (Northeast India, Indochina, Sundaland, Philippines) substantial areas of natural habitat have few wild animals (&gt;1 kg), bar a few hunting‐tolerant species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_hunting">Opposition to hunting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Opposition to hunting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2018</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_hunting" title="Opposition to hunting">Opposition to hunting</a></div>
<p>It has been argued by animal rights activists that killing animals for sport is unethical, cruel, and unnecessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> They note the suffering and cruelty inflicted on animals hunted for sport: "Many animals endure prolonged, painful deaths when they are injured but not killed by hunters ... Hunting disrupts migration and hibernation patterns and destroys families."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> Animal rights activists also comment that hunting is not needed to maintain an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological_balance" title="Ecological balance">ecological balance</a>, and that "nature takes care of its own".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> They say that hunting can be combated on public lands by "spread[ing] deer repellent or human hair (from barber shops) near hunting areas".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> Animal rights activists also argue that hunting is <a href="/wiki/Speciesism" title="Speciesism">speciesist</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote><p>Whether hunters try to justify their killing by citing human deaths caused by wild animals, by making conservationist claims, by claiming that it's acceptable to hunt as long as the animals' bodies are eaten, or simply because of the pleasure it brings them, the fact remains that hunting is morally unacceptable if we consider the interests of nonhuman animals. Hunted animals endure fear and pain, and then are deprived of their lives. Understanding the injustices of speciesism and the interests of nonhuman animals makes it clear that human pleasure cannot justify nonhuman animals' pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hunting_in_the_arts">Hunting in the arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunting&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Hunting in the arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1907" data-file-width="1110" decoding="async" height="378" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg/220px-Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg/330px-Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg/440px-Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Les_Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry_d%C3%A9cembre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limbourg_Brothers" title="Limbourg Brothers">Limbourg Brothers</a>, Boar hunt with hounds, <a href="/wiki/Illuminated_manuscript" title="Illuminated manuscript">illumination</a> from the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A8s_Riches_Heures_du_duc_de_Berry" title="Très Riches Heures du duc de Berry">Très Riches Heures du duc de Berry</a></i>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1445</span></div></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-Burch-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Burch_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"In North America and Eurasia the species has long been an important resource—in many areas <i>the</i> most important resource—for peoples inhabiting the northern <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">boreal forest</a> and tundra regions. Known human dependence on caribou/wild reindeer has a long history, beginning in the Middle Pleistocene (Banfield 1961:170; Kurtén 1968:170) and continuing to the present. […] The caribou/wild reindeer is thus an animal that has been a major resource for humans throughout a tremendous geographic area and across a time span of tens of thousands of years." <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFBurchJr1972">Burch, Ernest S.; Jr (1972). "The Caribou/Wild Reindeer as a Human Resource". <i>American Antiquity</i>. <b>37</b> (3): 339–68. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.2307%2F278435" rel="nofollow">10.2307/278435</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JSTOR_(identifier)" title="JSTOR (identifier)">JSTOR</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/278435" rel="nofollow">278435</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:161921691" rel="nofollow">161921691</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=American+Antiquity&amp;rft.atitle=The+Caribou%2FWild+Reindeer+as+a+Human+Resource&amp;rft.volume=37&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=339-68&amp;rft.date=1972&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A161921691%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F278435%23id-name%3DJSTOR&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.2307%2F278435&amp;rft.aulast=Burch&amp;rft.aufirst=Ernest+S.&amp;rft.au=Jr&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHunting"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
Machiavelli provides a rationale, if not the origin, of noble hunting:
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFMachiavelli1531"><a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Machiavelli" title="Niccolò Machiavelli">Machiavelli, Niccolò</a> (1531). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=r6lROQffJ7cC" rel="nofollow">"Discourses on the first decade of Titus Livius, Book 3"</a>.  In Gilbert, Allan (ed.). <i>Machiavelli: The Chief Works and Others</i>. Vol. 1. Duke University Press (published 1989). p. 516. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8223-8157-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8223-8157-0"><bdi>978-0-8223-8157-0</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 December</span> 2013</span>. <q>[...] hunting expeditions, as Xenophon makes plain, are images of war; therefore to men of rank such activity is honorable and necessary.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Discourses+on+the+first+decade+of+Titus+Livius%2C+Book+3&amp;rft.btitle=Machiavelli%3A+The+Chief+Works+and+Others&amp;rft.pages=516&amp;rft.pub=Duke+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1531&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8223-8157-0&amp;rft.aulast=Machiavelli&amp;rft.aufirst=Niccol%C3%B2&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dr6lROQffJ7cC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHunting"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFDunlap1999">Dunlap, Thomas R. Studies in Environment and History. Cambridge University Press. p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/natureenglishdia0000dunl/page/61" rel="nofollow">61</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-65700-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-65700-6"><bdi>978-0-521-65700-6</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">24 December</span> 2013</span>. <q>The settlers adopted sport hunting, as they did other elements of British culture, but they had to adapt it. Social circumstances and biological realities reshaped it and gave it new meaning. There was no elite monopolizing access to land. Indeed, the great attraction and boast of these nations were of land for all.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Remaking+Worlds%3A+European+models+in+New+Lands&amp;rft.btitle=Nature+and+the+English+Diaspora%3A+Environment+and+History+in+the+United+States%2C+Canada%2C+Australia%2C+and+New+Zealand&amp;rft.series=Studies+in+Environment+and+History&amp;rft.pages=61&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-65700-6&amp;rft.aulast=Dunlap&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas+R.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DUDaEZnZ093EC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHunting"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Brockington, Dan. <i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=hanwVhP-JFQC&amp;pg=PA47&amp;dq" rel="nofollow">Nature unbound: conservation, capitalism and the future of protected areas</a></i>, Earthscan, 2008.<br/> "The birth of the international conservation movement as we recognize it today was due to the influence of powerful aristocratic hunters who wished to preserve suitable specimens for their sport from the alleged depredations of Africans (Mackenzie, 1988). The international hunting fraternity remains a powerful force behind conservation today."</span>

<li id="cite_note-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-141">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFStokstad2019">Stokstad E (5 May 2019). <a class="external text" href="https://www.science.org/content/article/landmark-analysis-documents-alarming-global-decline-nature" rel="nofollow">"Landmark analysis documents the alarming global decline of nature"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">AAAS</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">10 May</span> 2021</span>. <q>For the first time at a global scale, the report has ranked the causes of damage. Topping the list, changes in land use—principally agriculture—that have destroyed habitat. Second, hunting and other kinds of exploitation. These are followed by climate change, pollution, and invasive species, which are being spread by trade and other activities. Climate change will likely overtake the other threats in the next decades, the authors note. Driving these threats are the growing human population, which has doubled since 1970 to 7.6 billion, and consumption. (Per capita of use of materials is up 15% over the past 5 decades.)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Science&amp;rft.atitle=Landmark+analysis+documents+the+alarming+global+decline+of+nature&amp;rft.date=2019-05-05&amp;rft.aulast=Stokstad&amp;rft.aufirst=E&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.science.org%2Fcontent%2Farticle%2Flandmark-analysis-documents-alarming-global-decline-nature&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHunting"></span></span>
